كتاب الصوم يوم ومتي التجنيس والمزيد رجل أصبح صائماً متطوعاً فدخل على أخ من إخوانه فسأله أن يفطر لا بأس بأن يفطر لقول النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: من أفطر لحق أخيه يكتب له ثواب صوم ألفي يوم قضى يوماً يكتب له ثواب صوم ألفي يوم ونقله أيضاً في التتارخانية والمحيط والمبسوط (وإذا أفطر) المتطوع على أي حال كان ( عليه القضاء) لا خلاف بين أصحابنا في وجوبه صيانة لما مضى عن البطلان إلا إذا شرع متطوعاً) بالصوم (في خمسة أيام يومي العيدين وأيام التشريق، فلا يلزمه قضاؤها بإفسادها في ظاهر الرواية عن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله لأن صومها مأمور بنقضه، ولم يجز إتمامه لأنه بنفس الشروع ارتكب المنهي عنه للإعراض عن ضيافة الله فأمر بقطعه وعن أبي يوسف ومحمد عليه القضاء يعني وإن وجب الفطر فيما ذكرنا إشارة إلى قضاء نفل الصلاة الذي قطعه بشروعه عند نحو الطلوع كما تقدم والله الموفق بمنه الأعظم للدين الأقوم.
(قال في التجنيس بيان للفائدة. قوله : (فسأله) ظاهره، ولو كان السؤال بغير يمين، وكذلك قوله في الحديث : لحق أخيه عام . قوله : (ثواب) صوم ألفي يوم أي غير الألف السابقة. قوله : (وإذا أفطر على أي حال كان سواء كان الفطر لعذر أم لا وسواء أفسده قصداً أم لا، وهذا إذا شرع قصداً فلو شرع فيه ظناً أنه عليه تذكر أنه ليس عليه شيء، فأفطر فوراً فلا قضاء عليه أما لو مضي ساعة لزمه القضاء لأنه يمضيها صار كأنه نوى في هذه الساعة أفاده في البحر، والمراد بالساعة القطعة من الزمن، وانظر ما لو تذكر أنه ليس عليه، ونوى قطعه إلا أنه لم يتعاط مفطراً هل يكون شارعاً، ومقتضى قولهم أنه بنية الفطر لا يكون مفطراً أنه لا يعد إفطاراً، أو يكون مشروعاً، وحرره قوله لا خلاف بين أصحابنا إلا في صائمة تطوعاً عرض عليها الحيض ففي القضاء خلاف، والأصح الوجوب . قوله (صيانة لما مضى أي من الشروع عن البطلان فإنه لما أعقب القضاء كان غير باطل بخلاف ما إذا لم يعقبه قوله: (وعن أبي يوسف ومحمد عليه لقضاء) لأنّ الشروع ملزم كالنذر كالشروع في الصلاة في الأوقات المكروهة، ووجه الفرق للإمام أن القضاء بالشروع يبتني على وجوب الإتمام وهو منتف لأنه بنفس الشروع يكون مرتكباً للنهي ، فأمر بقطعه بخلاف النذر حيث لم يصر مرتكباً للنهي بمجرد النذر لأنه التزم طاعة الله تعالى، وإنما المعصية بالفعل، وبخلاف الشروع في الصلاة في الأوقات المكروهة حيث لم يصر مرتكباً للنهي بمجرد الشروع، ولهذا لا يحنث به إن حلف لا يصلي ما لم يسجد، والشروع هو الموجب للقضاء دون الصلاة فصار كالنذر ولأنه يمكنه الأداء بذلك الشروع في الصلاة لا على وجه الكراهة بأن يمسك حتى تبيض الشمس زيلعي . قوله: (وفيما ذكرنا) أي من قوله : لأنه بنفس الشروع ارتكب المنهي عنه الخ فإنه لا يقال في الصلاة أنه بنفس الشروع فيها ارتكب المنهى عنه، بل إنما يكون ذلك بالسجود بدليل مسئلة اليمين. قوله : (عند نحو الطلوع هو الاستواء، والغروب والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم، وأستغفر الله العظيم.
Book of Fasting. Day and when. Al-Tajnīs and al-Mazīd: A man became a voluntary faster, then entered upon a brother from his brothers, and he asked him to break his fast. There is no harm in him breaking his fast, because of the Prophet's saying: 'Whoever breaks his fast for the sake of his brother, there is written for him the reward of fasting two thousand days.' He made up a day, and there is written for him the reward of fasting two thousand days. And it is also transmitted in al-Tatārkhāniyyah, al-Muḥīṭ, and al-Mabsūṭ. (And if he breaks his fast) the voluntary faster, in whatever state (then upon him is the making it up). There is no disagreement among our companions concerning its obligation, to preserve what has passed from nullification, except if he began a voluntary fast on five days: the two days of Eid and the days of al-Tashrīq. Then making them up is not obligatory upon him by spoiling them in the apparent transmission from Abū Ḥanīfah, may Allah have mercy on him, because its fast is commanded to be broken, and it is not permissible to complete it, because by the very commencement he engaged in the prohibited due to turning away from the hospitality of Allah, so he was commanded to cut it. And from Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad, upon him is the making it up. Meaning, even if breaking the fast is obligatory in what we mentioned, it is an indication of making up the supererogatory prayer which he cut off by commencing it around sunrise, as has preceded. And Allah grants success with His greatest grace for the most upright religion. (He said in al-Tajnīs an explanation of the benefit. His statement: 'he asked him' is apparent, even if the asking was without an oath. Likewise his statement in the hadith: 'for the sake of his brother' is general. His statement: 'reward of fasting two thousand days' meaning other than the previous thousand. His statement: 'And if he breaks his fast' in whatever state, whether the breaking was for an excuse or not, and whether he spoiled it intentionally or not. This is if he began intentionally. If he began thinking that he owed a fast, then remembered that nothing was upon him, and broke immediately, then there is no making up upon him. However, if he passed an hour, he must make it up because by passing it he became as if he intended during that hour. This was useful in al-Baḥr. And the meaning of 'hour' is a portion of time. Consider if he remembered that nothing was upon him and intended to cut it, but he did not consume any nullifier: would he be considered as having commenced? And the implication of their statement that by the intention of breaking he is not a breaker? That it is not counted as breaking, or that he is a commencer? And he edited it. His statement: there is no disagreement among our companions except concerning a woman who began a voluntary fast and then menstruation came to her, then there is disagreement concerning making it up, and the correct view is obligation. His statement: 'to preserve what has passed' meaning the commencement from nullification, because when he made it up, it was not invalid, contrary to when he did not make it up. His statement: 'And from Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad, upon him is the making it up' because the commencement is binding like a vow, like commencement of prayer in disliked times. And the face of the difference for the Imam is that making up by commencement is based on the obligation of completion, and that is negated because by the very commencement he becomes a committer of the prohibited, so he was commanded to cut it, contrary to a vow where he does not become a committer of the prohibited by merely vowing, because he undertook obedience to Allah, and disobedience is only by the act. And contrary to commencement of prayer in disliked times where he does not become a committer of the prohibited by merely commencing, and for this reason he does not break an oath if he swore not to pray, as long as he does not prostrate. And the commencement is what necessitates making up, not the prayer itself, so it becomes like a vow. And because he can perform it by that commencement in prayer without the disliked aspect, by waiting until the sun whitens. [al-Zaylaʿī]. His statement: 'And in what we mentioned' meaning from his statement: 'because by the very commencement he engaged in the prohibited, etc.' For it is not said in prayer that by the very commencement he engaged in the prohibited, rather that only happens by prostration, as evidenced by the case of the oath. His statement: 'around sunrise' is the zenith, and the setting. And Allah, the Glorious and Exalted, knows best. And I seek forgiveness from Allah the Almighty.
Source pages p. 691

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya of al-Tahtawi addresses the ruling of breaking a voluntary (nafl) fast and the necessity of qada (making it up). The author begins by stating that a voluntary faster who breaks his fast, for any reason (whether with a valid excuse or not, intentionally or unintentionally), must make it up. This is agreed upon among the Hanafis to preserve the validity of what has already been performed. An exception is made for five days: the two Eid days and the three days of Tashriq (11th, 12th, 13th of Dhul Hijjah). According to the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya) from Imam Abu Hanifa, if one begins a voluntary fast on these days and then breaks it, no qada is required because fasting on these days is inherently prohibited; the commencement itself is disobedience, so the act is commanded to be cut off. However, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that qada is obligatory even in these days, drawing an analogy with the commencement of a nafl prayer at a disliked time, which requires qada if broken. The author then elaborates on details: if one mistakenly thought he owed a fast and then realized his error, if he breaks immediately, no qada; if he delays for a period, qada is due. The commentary also discusses the hadith cited as proof for the permissibility of breaking a fast for a brother's sake, noting that the reward is for the intention, and that the request need not be an oath. The intra-Hanafi dispute is clearly presented: Abu Hanifa's view (no qada on the five days) and the Sahibayn's view (qada required), with the author noting that the relied-upon position is given in the text. The passage guards against the misunderstanding that all voluntary fasts, once begun, are irrevocable without qada.

Key Terms
القضاء (al-qadā'): Making up a missed act of worship after its prescribed time; here specifically for a broken voluntary fast.
الشروع (al-shurū'): The commencement of an act of worship; in this context, beginning a voluntary fast or prayer.
أيام التشريق (ayyām al-tashrīq): The three days following Eid al-Adha (11th, 12th, 13th of Dhul Hijjah) when fasting is prohibited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the apparent transmission (zahir al-riwaya) from Imam Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling on qada for a voluntary fast broken on the day of Eid al-Fitr?
A) Qada is obligatory.
B) Qada is not obligatory.
C) Qada is recommended but not required.
D) The fast is invalid without qada.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a broken voluntary fast generally requires qada, but according to Imam Abu Hanifa, no qada is needed if the fast was begun on one of the five prohibited days because the commencement itself is an act of disobedience.

Validity of Vows and Fasting on Prohibited Days
Explains which vows are valid and specifically vowing to fast on Eid and Tashreeq days.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which vows are valid in Hanafi fiqh and explain why a vow to fast on Eid or Tashreeq is considered valid despite the prohibition, applying the principle of nahy li-ghayrihi.

Core Idea
A vow to fast on Eid is valid because the prohibition is external (li-ghayrihi), not intrinsic.

Vows (nadhr) are a way of obligating oneself to an act of worship. The Hanafi school carefully distinguishes which vows are binding. This lesson explores the general principles of valid vows and then focuses on a specific case: vowing to fast on the prohibited days of Eid and Tashreeq. Understanding the concept of 'extrinsic prohibition' (nahy li-ghayrihi) is key to resolving this seemingly contradictory ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon (e.g., a vow to fast on Eid) and what the hukm is (sahih/batil).
2
Locate the dalil
What proof is cited? The hadith 'Kaffarat al-nadhr kaffarat al-yamin' is used for unintended conditional vows.
Also consider the qiyas used for i'tikaf and Hajj walking.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith support the rule? It equates the expiation of a vow to that of an oath, giving a choice for unintended conditional vows.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
What is the intra-Hanafi dispute on vowing to fast on prohibited days? The preferred opinion says valid; a narration from Ibn al-Mubarak and Zufar says invalid.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Why is the validity opinion preferred? The prohibition is extrinsic (nahy li-ghayrihi), so it does not negate the legality of the act.
This is based on usul al-fiqh principles.

كتاب الصوم

وهو المريض، والميت والناذر إنما يلتزم بنذره ما يكون مشروعاً حقاً الله تعالى مقصوداً (ولا) يصح نذر (الواجبات) لأن إيجاب الواجب محال (بنذرها) لما بينا (ويصح) النذر (بالعتق) يعني الاعتاق لافتراض التحرير في الكفارات نصاً (والاعتكاف) لأنّ جنسه واجباً، من القعدة الأخير في الصلاة فأصل المكث بهذه الصفة له نظير في الشرع، والاعتكاف انتظار للصلاة فهو كالجالس في الصلاة فإذن صح نذره والحج ماشياً لأنّ من قرب من مكة يلزمه ماشياً فالمشي بصفة مخصوصة له نظير في الشرع، ويصح نذر العبد والمرأة الاعتكاف، وللسيد والزوج المنع فيقضيانه بعد العتق والإبانة وليس للمولى منع المكاتب (و) كذا يصح نذر الصلاة) غير المفروضة والصوم) والتصدق بالمال والذبح لظهور جنسها شرعاً مثل الأضحية (فإن نذر) مكلف (نذراً) مما بشيء يصح نذره وكان (مطلقاً) غير مقيد بوجود شيء كقوله : الله علي أو نذر الله علي صلاة ركعتين (أو معلقاً بشرط) يريد كونه كقوله : إن رزقني الله غلاماً فعلي إطعام عشرة مساكين ووجد الشرط الزمه الوفاء به) لما تلونا وروينا، وأما إذا علق النذر بما لا يريد كونه كقوله : إن كلمت زيداً فلله علي عتق رقبة ثم كلمه فإنه يتخير بين الوفاء بما نذره من العتق وبين كفارة يمين على الصحيح وهو المفتي به لقوله : كفارة النذر كفارة اليمين وحمل على ما ذكرناه (وصح نذر صوم) يومي العيدين وأيام التشريق لأنّ النهي عن صومها يحقق تصور الصوم منهياً ضرورة والنهي لغيره لا ينافي المشروعية فصح نذره في المختار) وفي رواية لا : يصح لأنه نذر بمعصية قلنا
Book of Fasting. It is the sick, the dead, and the one who makes a vow only obligates himself by his vow to what is prescribed as a right of Allah the Exalted intended. (And) the vow of (obligatory acts) is not valid, because making obligatory what is already obligatory is impossible (by vowing them) due to what we have explained. (And) the vow (of freeing a slave) is valid, meaning freeing, because the obligation of emancipation in expiations is textually established. (And i'tikaf) because its type is obligatory, like the last sitting in prayer, so the original staying in this manner has a parallel in the law, and i'tikaf is waiting for prayer, so it is like one sitting in prayer, thus his vow is valid. And (vowing) Hajj while walking is valid, because whoever is near Mecca is required to walk, so walking in a specific manner has a parallel in the law. And the vow of i'tikaf by a slave and a woman is valid, but the master and husband may prevent, and they make it up after emancipation and divorce. The master may not prevent a mukatib. (And) likewise, the vow of prayer (other than obligatory) and fasting and charity with wealth and slaughtering are valid, because their type appears in the law like the sacrifice. If a legally responsible person makes a vow (of something valid to vow) and it is (absolute) not tied to the occurrence of something, like his saying: 'Upon me is Allah' or 'By Allah, upon me is a prayer of two rak'ahs' (or conditional upon a condition) meaning its occurrence, like his saying: 'If Allah grants me a son, then upon me is feeding ten poor people' and the condition occurs, fulfillment is incumbent upon him, based on what we have recited and narrated. As for when he ties the vow to what he does not intend to occur, like his saying: 'If I speak to Zayd, then upon me is freeing a slave' and then he speaks to him, then he has a choice between fulfilling what he vowed of freeing and the expiation of an oath according to the correct opinion, which is the mufta bihi, due to his saying: 'The expiation of a vow is the expiation of an oath,' and it is interpreted as we have mentioned. (And the vow of fasting) the two days of Eid and the days of Tashreeq is valid, because the prohibition of fasting them necessarily actualizes the conceptualization of fasting as prohibited, and the prohibition for something else does not negate legality, so his vow is valid in the chosen opinion. And in one narration: it is not valid, because it is a vow of disobedience. We say:
Source pages p. 694

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the rulings of vows (nadhr) in the Hanafi school. It begins by stating that a vow is only valid for acts that are legally recognized as devotional (mashru'). Vows to perform already obligatory acts (wajibat) are invalid because one cannot impose what is already required. Vows to free slaves, perform i'tikaf, perform Hajj while walking, pray supererogatory prayers, fast, give charity, and slaughter animals are valid because their types have a basis in the Shari'ah (e.g., emancipation in kaffarat, i'tikaf analogous to sitting in prayer). The vow of a slave or woman to perform i'tikaf is valid but subject to permission of master or husband; they must make it up if prevented. A mukatib (slave on contract of manumission) is not prevented by his master. The text then distinguishes between absolute vows and conditional vows: if the vow is conditional on something the person intends (e.g., if Allah grants a son), fulfillment is obligatory upon occurrence. If conditional on something not intended (e.g., if I speak to Zayd), the person has a choice between fulfilling the vow or giving the expiation of an oath (kaffarat yamin), which is the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) based on the hadith 'Kaffarat al-nadhr kaffarat al-yamin'. Finally, it addresses a specific case: vowing to fast on the days of Eid and Tashreeq. The preferred opinion is that such a vow is valid because the prohibition is not due to the essence of fasting but due to neglecting the feast (a secondary reason). The act of fasting is conceptually possible despite the prohibition, so the vow is binding. The opposing narration (from Ibn al-Mubarak) holds it invalid as a vow of disobedience. The Hanafi response (implied) is that the prohibition is extrinsic, so it does not negate validity.

Key Terms
النذر (al-nadhr): A vow by which a person obligates upon themselves an act of worship for the sake of Allah.
المختار (al-mukhtar): The chosen or preferred opinion within the Hanafi school.
النهي لغيره (al-nahy li-ghayrihi): A prohibition that is not due to the essence of the act itself but due to an external factor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi opinion, what is the ruling on a person who vows to fast on the day of Eid al-Fitr?
A) The vow is invalid because it is a vow of disobedience.
B) The vow is valid and the person must fast that day.
C) The person has a choice between fasting and giving kaffarah.
D) The vow is valid but the person cannot fulfill it due to prohibition.

Key Takeaway
A vow to fast on Eid or Tashreeq is valid in the Hanafi school because the prohibition is extrinsic, making the act conceptually possible and binding.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
8 min
Vowing to Fast on Prohibited Days: Validity and Nullification of Specifications
Intra-Hanafi dispute on validity of vow to fast on Eid and Tashreeq days

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi chosen view on the validity of a vow to fast on prohibited days and apply the rule of nullification of specifications (ilgha' al-ta'yin) to unconditional vows.

Core Idea
A vow to fast on Eid is valid because the prohibition is external; specifications in vows are nullified.

In this lesson, we examine a subtle intra-Hanafi dispute: can a person validly vow to fast on the two Eids and the days of Tashreeq? The prohibition of fasting on these days is clear, but does it render a related vow invalid? We will analyze the reasoning behind the chosen view (al-mukhtar) and understand the broader principle that specifications of time, place, and recipient in unconditional vows are not binding.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
Recognize that there are two views within the Hanafi school: one considers the vow valid (sahih), the other invalid due to being a vow of disobedience. Determine which is the mufta bihi.
The source explicitly states 'fasha nidhruhu fi al-mukhtar'.
2
Understand the reasoning for validity
Analyze why the chosen view holds the vow valid: the prohibition of fasting on these days is for an external reason (turning away from Allah's hospitality), not because the act of fasting is inherently evil. The act itself remains a qurbah.
The analogy with prayer in usurped land is key.
3
Apply the principle of nullification of specifications
Learn that in unconditional vows, any specification of time, place, coin, or recipient is nullified. The vow creates an obligation in the dhimmah that can be fulfilled in any equivalent manner.
This is distinct from suspended vows where the condition must occur.
4
Determine practical consequences
If someone vows to fast Sha'ban and instead fasts Rajab, the vow is fulfilled. Similarly, if one vows to fast on Eid, the vow is valid but the fast is sinful.
The source gives the example of Rajab substituting for Sha'ban.

عنه بقوله : ولذلك قوله : (عن) ضيافة (الكريم أي ولا عذر لمن تأخر عنها بخلاف ضيافة البخيل، فإنه قد يتأبى عنها لأن طعام البخيل داء قوله : (أجزأه مع الحرمة) انظر هل يثاب على صومها فيكون للفعل جهتان، أو لا يثاب أصلاً نظراً للعارض وقد تقدم ما فيه، ولا فرق في الحكم المذكور بين أن بذكر المنهي بأن قال: نذرت صوم النحر أولاً كأنه قال غد: فوافق يوم النحر، ولو نذر صوم الأضحى، وأفطر وقضى صح زاهدي، ولو صام فيها ولو معيناً لا يختص بزمان، ومكان ودرهم وفقير فلو نذر التصدق يوم الجمعة بمكة بهذا الدرهم على فلان فخالف جاز، وكذا لو عجل قبله فلو، عين شهراً للإعتكاف، أو للصوم فعجل قبله عنه صح، وكذا لو نذر أن سنة كذا فحج سنة قبلها صح أو صلاة يوم كذا فصلاها قبله لأنه تعجيل بعد وجود السبب، وهو النذر فيلغو التعيين شرنبلالية، فليحفظ بخلاف النذر المعلق فإنه لا يجوز تعجيله قبل وجود الشرط . قوله : (في اللمة) متعلق سن.
Book of Fasting: [If someone says] 'for Allah a slave' then upon him is feeding ten poor people, and if the condition is found, fulfillment is obligatory upon him, as we have recited and narrated. As for when he suspends the vow on something he does not want to happen, like saying: If I speak to Zaid, then for Allah upon me is freeing a slave, then he speaks to him, then he has the choice between fulfilling what he vowed of freeing and between the expiation of an oath, according to the correct view and it is the one given for fatwa, due to his statement: 'The expiation of a vow is the expiation of an oath.' And it is interpreted upon what we mentioned. And the vow of fasting the two Eid days and the days of Tashreeq is valid, because the prohibition of fasting them confirms the conceptualization of fasting as prohibited necessarily, and the prohibition for other than itself does not contradict legitimacy, so his vow is valid in the chosen view. And in one narration: it is not valid because it is a vow of disobedience. We said: from what we recited from the verse and narrated the hadith, and he mentioned them at the beginning of the chapter. His statement: due to his statement, peace be upon him, and because it is a vow outwardly an oath in meaning, because his intention is prevention, so he has choice necessarily. He said in al-Bahr: after quoting, know that this detail, even though it is the statement of the verifiers, has no basis in transmission, because what is mentioned in zahir al-riwaya is the obligation of fulfilling the vowed thing whether immediate or suspended. In the narration of nawadir he has choice between expiation of an oath and fulfillment. He said in al-Khulasa: and with this fatwa is given. So it results that the fatwa is on choice absolutely, as such in the handwriting of some virtuous ones, transmitted by Abu al-Su'ud in his hashia on al-Ashbah. And before him he mentioned that the choice is with respect to what is like hajj, or fasting, or charity, meaning as for when it is by way of suspending divorce, manumission, and ila, then the suspended occurs only, and there is no choice. His statement: 'and interpreted upon what we mentioned' i.e. of the suspended vow on a condition he does not want to happen. His statement: 'confirms the conceptualization of fasting as prohibited necessarily' and that is because if the prohibited act is not conceivable from a person, there is no basis for its prohibition, because it is not within his capability. So it is not said to a eunuch: do not commit adultery, nor to a blind person: do not see, due to the impossibility of the prohibited act from them. His statement: 'the prohibition for other than itself' – prohibition is a verbal noun in the sense of passive participle, and its referent here is fasting these days, and the referent of 'other' is turning away. And the meaning: the prohibited for other than itself i.e. not for its own essence does not contradict the legitimacy of that prohibited. His statement: 'does not contradict legitimacy' i.e. it does not prevent validity, like a sale at the first call on Friday, for it is prohibited due to negligence of the call, but if it is contracted it is valid. And the intended meaning of legitimacy is not that it is legally demanded, for the prohibited due to hospitality, with striving, and fasting here is not an act of worship essentially, as evidenced by its validity from a disbeliever. And the condition for the validity of a vow is that it be not an act of disobedience. And reward is not necessitated for him. And it is probable that the intended meaning of legitimacy is that it is legally demanded, so he is rewarded for it, and the fasting of these days has two aspects: the aspect of fulfilling the command in His statement: 'And let them fulfill their vows' (al-Hajj 22:29), and in this respect it is an act of worship for which he is rewarded; and the aspect of performing it on these days which necessitates turning away, and in this respect it is forbidden. Its analogy is prayer in usurped land, and the owner of al-Nahr has preceded what indicates that. And the statement of the sharh after we said: 'disobedience due to the meaning of turning away from the hospitality of Allah, so it does not prevent validity' points to the first meaning. His statement: 'so his vow is valid' i.e. the vow of fasting on these days, and it is a verbal noun annexed to its object. His statement: 'and in one narration' it is the narration of Ibn al-Mubarak from the Imam, and with it said Zufar. His statement: from him, and the validity of the vow does not necessitate it being an act of worship for which he is rewarded, for it is valid with freeing, and it is from these. Validity does not prevent approval. Book of Fasting: from its essence (and) therefore disobedience due to the meaning of turning away from the hospitality of Allah, so (it is not obligatory to break it) in compliance with the command, lest by fasting it he become one who turns away (and it is obligatory to make it up) due to the validity of the vow considering the origin (and if he fasts it, it suffices for the fasting of the vow) along with the prohibition (resulting from turning away from the hospitality of Allah (and we nullify) the specification of time and specification of (place and) specification of (the dirham and) specification of (the poor person) because the vow is an obligation of the act in the dhimmah from the perspective of it being a drawing near, not by virtue of its occurrence in a time, place, and poor person, and specifying it is for estimation or deferment. (So the fasting of the month of Rajab suffices him for his vow of fasting Sha'ban) because the cause exists, which is the vow and the drawing near of subduing the self, not by its occurrence in a specific month, and in its acceleration there is benefit for him in acquiring reward that might be lost by his death or the occurrence of a preventing factor before the arrival of the time. (It is not valid) because it is a vow of disobedience. In this narration, he considered the accidental factor that necessitated the prohibition, and in zahir al-riwaya he considered its origin and ruled validity. His statement: 'due to the meaning of turning away' – the genitive is for explanation. His statement: 'and therefore' i.e. because its fasting is disobedience due to the meaning of turning away etc. His statement: 'in compliance with the command' i.e. derived from the prohibition, for the prohibition of a thing is a command for its opposite, according to the dispute about it. And the Prophet, peace be upon him, prohibited fasting the day of Fitr as in Sahih, and in Mu'jam al-Tabarani from Ibn Abbas that the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, sent a caller in the days of Mina shouting: Do not fast these days, for they are days of eating, drinking, and ba'al i.e. intercourse with women. His statement: 'lest by fasting it he become' etc. is the reason for the obligation of breaking the fast, and it could be dispensed with by his statement: 'and therefore'. His statement: 'from the hospitality of the Generous' i.e. there is no excuse for one who falls behind from it, unlike the hospitality of the miser, for he may abstain from it because the miser's food is disease. His statement: 'it suffices him with prohibition' – consider: is he rewarded for his fasting so that the act has two aspects, or is he not rewarded at all considering the accidental factor? And what was previously stated about it is there. And there is no difference in the mentioned ruling between his mentioning the prohibited by saying: I vowed the fasting of Nahr (sacrifice) or not, like if he said: tomorrow, and it coincides with the day of Nahr. And if he vowed fasting the day of Adha and broke and made it up, it is valid (Zahidi). And if he fasts on these days for another obligatory, like make-up or expiation, it is not valid because what is in the dhimmah is perfect, performing it deficiently – transmitted by al-Sayyid. His statement: 'and we nullify the specification of time etc.' He said in al-Tanwir and its commentary: and the vow of i'tikaf, or prayer, or fasting, or others, not suspended, even if specified, is not particularized to a time, place, dirham, and poor person. So if he vowed to give charity on Friday in Mecca with this dirham to so-and-so, and he violated, it is permissible. Likewise if he advanced it before. So if he specified a month for i'tikaf or for fasting and advanced it before, it is valid. Likewise if he vowed to perform hajj in a certain year and performed hajj the year before, it is valid. Or prayer on a certain day and performed it before, because it is acceleration after the existence of the cause, which is the vow, so the specification is nullified (Sharnabalaliyya). So memorize it, unlike the suspended vow, for it is not permissible to accelerate it before the existence of the condition. His statement: 'in the dhimmah' is attached to obligation. His statement: 'and its specification' i.e. time, and the rest are analogized to it. His statement: 'so the fasting of the month of Rajab suffices him' etc. He mentioned the form of advancement, and did not mention the form of delay, and apparently it is likewise due to lack of specification, or there is no sin. His statement: 'or' a preventing factor like illness or old age.
Source pages p. 695

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi deals with two related issues: (1) the validity of an unconditional vow (nadhr) to fast on prohibited days (Eid al-Fitr, Eid al-Adha, and days of Tashreeq), and (2) the general principle that specification of time, place, coin, or recipient in a vow is nullified unless the vow is suspended on a condition. The commentary refines the earlier text of Maraqi al-Falah and al-Durr al-Mukhtar, presenting an intra-Hanafi dispute between the chosen view (al-mukhtar) and another narration attributed to Ibn al-Mubarak and Zufar. In the chosen view, a vow to fast on these days is valid because the prohibition is due to an external reason (turning away from Allah's hospitality) not inherent in the act of fasting itself. The fasting is still a form of worship in its essence (qurbah) but becomes sinful due to the time. Therefore, if one fasts on these days for the vow, it counts but with sin. The other narration considers it a vow of disobedience and thus invalid. The relied-upon fatwa (mufta bihi) is the chosen view, i.e., validity. Importantly, the text also clarifies that if such a vow is made, it is not obligatory to break the fast immediately; rather, one must fast and then make it up later. The reason for not obligating immediate breaking is that the command to break is derived from the prohibition, but the prohibition here is not absolute. The passage then discusses the nullification of specifications (ilgha' al-ta'yin) in vows: when someone vows a specific time (e.g., fasting in Sha'ban) or place (e.g., giving charity in Mecca) or specific coin or poor person, those specifications are ignored because the vow is in the dhimmah (obligation upon oneself) of the act as a general act of worship. Thus, one can fulfill it at a different time or place. This principle applies to unconditional (ghayr mu'allaq) vows only; suspended vows (mu'allaq) must be fulfilled only after the condition occurs. The text gives the example: if one vows to fast Sha'ban but fasts Rajab, it suffices. The rationale is that the cause (sabab) of the vow is the act of vowing itself, and acceleration is beneficial to secure reward before death or impediments.

Key Terms
النذر (al-nadhr): A vow to perform an act of worship (qurbah) that is otherwise not obligatory, made binding by one's own statement.
المختار (al-mukhtar): The chosen and relied-upon view among Hanafi scholars, as opposed to other narrations.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The transmitted rulings from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani in his six well-known books (the zahir al-riwayah).
النهي لغيره (al-nahy li-ghayrihi): A prohibition that is not for the essence of the act itself but for an external reason or attribute.
إلغاء التعيين (ilgha' al-ta'yin): The nullification of specifications (time, place, coin, recipient) in unconditional vows.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (al-mukhtar), what is the ruling if someone vows to fast on the day of Eid al-Fitr?
A) The vow is invalid because fasting on Eid is forbidden.
B) The vow is valid; he must fast that day and it counts for his vow, but he commits a sin.
C) The vow is valid but he must break the fast immediately and make it up on another day without sin.
D) The vow is valid only if he did not specify the day; otherwise it is invalid.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a vow to fast on prohibited days is valid (mukhtar), and specifications in unconditional vows are not binding.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
8 min
A Woman's Conditional Vow to Pray in the Sacred Mosque: The Hanafi Debate
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the fulfillment of a conditional vow to pray in a specific mosque.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi majority view that a woman who vows to pray in the Sacred Mosque fulfills her vow by praying at home, and contrast it with Imam Zufar's view.

Core Idea
A vow's fulfillment is judged by the intention behind the act, not the literal wording.

This lesson examines a specific case where a woman vows to pray in the Sacred Mosque. The Hanafi majority, unlike Imam Zufar, considers that she can fulfill her vow by praying in the darkest part of her house, since the best prayer for a woman is at home and the vow was motivated by the reward of prayer.

Guided Path
1
State the case and the two positions
Identify that a woman vowed to pray in the Sacred Mosque. Then note that Imam Zufar says she must pray there, while the majority of Hanafis (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) say she can pray at home and the vow is fulfilled.
The case is about a suspended (conditional) vow, as clarified in the commentary.
2
Identify the proof of the majority
The majority rely on the hadith that the best prayer for a woman is in the darkest part of her house. Since the woman's vow was motivated by reward, and the best reward for her is at home, praying at home fulfills the intended reward. The location was merely a means, not an end.
This is a talil (cause-based reasoning) that the essence of the vow is the act of prayer, not the physical location.
3
Identify Zufar's proof
Imam Zufar holds that the literal wording of the vow specified the Sacred Mosque, so the location is part of the obligation. He does not consider the woman's optimal prayer location.
Zufar's argument is based on the literal meaning (haqiqah) of the vow.
4
Apply the tarjih mechanism
The majority's view is preferred because it aligns with the purpose of the vow (reward) and the general principle that vows are interpreted according to intent (niyyah). The mufta bihi is the majority opinion.
The text indicates Zufar's view is a minority.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Zufar's view, the woman must travel to Makkah to pray in the Sacred Mosque to fulfill her vow. Under the majority, she can pray at home, which is easier and more rewarding for her.
This practical difference matters for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصوم
سئل عن أفضل صلاة المرأة فقال : في أشد مكان من بيتها ظلمة. فعلى هذا ينبغي أنها إذا التزمت الصلاة في المسجد الحرام بالنذر فصلت في أشد مكان من بيتها ظلمة تخرج عن موجب نذرها على ما يقوله زفر رحمه الله وإن على الناذر النذر بشرط) كقوله : إن قدم زيد فلله علي أن أتصدق بكذا لا يجزيه عنه ما فعله قبل وجود شرطه) لأن المعلق بالشرط عدم قبل وجوده وإنما يجوز الأداء بعد وجود السبب الذي علق النذر به والله المنان بفضله.

قوله: (فعلى هذا الخ) لا يظهر إلا في النذر المعلق أما غير المعلق لا يختص بمكان، كما قدمه قريباً. قوله : ( عن موجب بفتح الجيم. قوله : ( على ما يقوله زفر) أما على قول غيره فتخرج عنه بصلاتها في أي مكان كان وفيه أن زفر يقول بالتعيين من غير نظر لكثرة الثواب كما هو المتبادر عنه. قوله: (لا يجزيه عنه ما فعله قبل وجود شرطه بقي ما لو وجد الشرط هل يتعين الزمان والمكان والفقير والدرهم والظاهر نعملها في التنوير، ثم إن علقه بشرط يريده [؟] كان قدم غائبي يوفي إن وجدا هـ، فإنه لا يكون موفياً إلا إذا كان على الوجه المذكور في نذره .

تتمة: النذر لا يدخل تحت الحكم، ولو بعتق رقبة في ملكة نذر أن يذبح ولده فعليه شاة لقصة الخليل عليه السلام نذر أن يتصدق بعشرة دراهم من الخبز فتصدق بغيره جاز إن ساوى العشرة كتصدقه بثمنه قال : على نذر ولم يزد عليه، ولا نية له فعليه كفارة يمين فإن وصل به المشيئة بطل لأنها تبطل كل ما تعلق بالقول عبادة، أو معاملة قال إن ذهبت هذه العلة فعلى كذا، فذهبت ثم عادت لا يلزمه شيء ا هـ من التنوير، وشرحه من الإيمان، وفيهما من عوارض الصوم، واعلم أن صيغة النذر تحتمل اليمين، فلذا كانت ست صور ذكرها بقوله : فإن لم ينو بنذره الصوم شيئاً، أو نوى النذر فقط أي من غير تعرض لليمين، أو نوى النذر ونوى أن لا يكون يميناً كان في هذه الصور نذراً فقط إجماعاً عملاً بالصيغة، وإن نوى اليمين، وأن لا يكون نذراً كان يميناً إجماعاً، وعليه كفارة يمين أن أفطر، وإن نواهما، أو نوى اليمين من غير تعرض للنذر كان نذراً، ويميناً حتى لو أفطر يجب القضاء للنذر، والكفارة لليمين عملاً بعموم المجاز خلافاً للثاني، والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم، وأستغفر الله العظيم.
Book of Fasting. He was asked about the best prayer of a woman, so he said: In the darkest place of her house. Based on this, it is fitting that if she obligated herself to prayer in the Sacred Mosque by a vow, and then prayed in the darkest place of her house, she would exit from the requirement of her vow according to what Zufar says, may Allah have mercy on him. And concerning the one who makes a vow conditional, like his saying: If Zayd arrives, then for Allah upon me that I give charity with such-and-such, it does not suffice him what he did before the existence of its condition, because what is suspended on a condition is non-existent before its existence, and performance is only permitted after the existence of the cause by which the vow was conditioned. And Allah is the Bestower by His grace. His saying: ('upon this etc.') is not apparent except in the suspended vow; as for the unconditional, it is not restricted to a place, as previously mentioned. His saying: ('about requirement') with a fatha on the jim. His saying: ('according to what Zufar says') as for according to the saying of others, she would exit from it by her prayer in any place, and in it that Zufar says specificity without regard for abundance of reward, as is apparent from him. His saying: ('it does not suffice him what he did before the existence of its condition') the remainder: if the condition exists, is the time, place, poor person, and dirham specified? Apparently we will act on it in al-Tanwir. Then if he conditioned it with a condition he wants, [؟] he had set a missing one, he fulfills if they are found, then he is only fulfilling if it is as mentioned in his vow. Appendix: The vow does not enter under a ruling, even if freeing a slave in his possession, a vow to slaughter his son, upon him a sheep due to the story of al-Khalil (peace be upon him). A vow to give charity with ten dirhams of bread, then he gave charity with other than it, it is permissible if it equals the ten, like his giving charity with its price. He said: upon a vow and did not add to it, and he had no intention, then upon him is the expiation of an oath. If he appended the will to it, it is void because it voids everything connected to speech, worship or transaction. He said: If this ailment goes away, then upon me such-and-such, then it went away and returned, nothing is required of him. Ended from al-Tanwir and its commentary from al-Iman, and in them from the impediments of fasting. And know that the formula of vow bears the meaning of oath, hence there are six forms mentioned by his saying: If he did not intend by his vow anything of fasting, or he intended only the vow, i.e., without reference to an oath, or he intended the vow and intended that it not be an oath, then in these forms it is only a vow by consensus, acting on the formula. And if he intended the oath and that it not be a vow, it is an oath by consensus, and upon him is the expiation of an oath if he breaks his fast. And if he intended both, or he intended the oath without reference to the vow, it is a vow and an oath, so that if he breaks his fast, qada is required for the vow and expiation for the oath, acting on the generality of metonymy, contrary to the second. And Allah Most High knows best, and I seek forgiveness from Allah the Magnificent.
Source pages p. 698

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya on Maraqi al-Falah discusses two interrelated topics: conditional vows (al-nadhr al-mu'allaq) and the effect of intention on whether a formula constitutes a vow or an oath. The text begins with a previous ruling that a woman's best prayer is in the darkest part of her house. It then extends this to a case where a woman vows to pray in the Sacred Mosque: according to Zufar, she must pray in the mosque; others say any dark place suffices because the vow was for reward, not location. The commentary clarifies that this only applies to suspended vows. Next, the conditional vow is defined: if someone says 'If Zayd comes, I must give charity,' the vow does not take effect until the condition is met; any charity before that is not fulfillment. The commentary then raises the issue of specification of time, place, and recipient when the condition is met. A 'tatmimah' (appendix) lists various rulings: a vow to do something already owned (e.g., free a slave) is invalid; a vow to slaughter a son requires a sheep (by analogy to Ibrahim); substituting like items in charity is permissible; a vow without intention requires oath expiation; tying a vow to will or conditional statements is void. Finally, the central discussion: the word 'nadhr' can be ambiguous between vow and oath. Six scenarios of intention are listed, with the four madhhab rulings across the first three (vow only) and last three (various combinations). The relied-upon position is that if both are intended, or only the oath is intended without mention of nadhr, the formula is both a vow and an oath, requiring both qada and expiation. This is a classic Hanafi treatment of ambiguity (ishtirak) in legal language.

Key Terms
النذر (al-nadhr): A verbal commitment to perform an act of worship (like prayer, fasting, charity) which becomes obligatory upon fulfillment of any condition or immediately if unconditional.
النذر المعلق (al-nadhr al-mu'allaq): A vow that is suspended on a condition, e.g., 'If Zayd arrives, then I will give charity.' It becomes binding only upon fulfillment of the condition.
زفر (Zufar): Imam Zufar ibn al-Hudhayl, a prominent Hanafi jurist known for his stricter interpretations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) Hanafi position, if a woman vows to pray in the Sacred Mosque, she can fulfill her vow by praying:
A) In any mosque
B) In the darkest part of her house
C) Only in the Sacred Mosque
D) She cannot fulfill it if she does not go

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the fulfillment of a conditional vow is determined by the underlying intent for reward, not the literal wording, as seen in the case of a woman's vow to pray in the Sacred Mosque.

The Six Scenarios of Intention in Nadhr: When is a Vow an Oath?
Analysis of the six intentions for the ambiguous formula of nadhr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the six possible intentions in a nadhr formulation and determine whether the resulting obligation is a vow, an oath, or both, with appropriate consequences.

Core Idea
The ambiguous formula of nadhr can be a vow, an oath, or both, depending solely on the speaker's intention.

In Hanafi fiqh, the word 'nadhr' can mean either a vow (obligation of worship) or an oath (requiring expiation if broken). Intention (niyyah) is decisive. This lesson walks through the six scenarios: three where it is only a vow (by consensus), one where it is only an oath (by consensus), and two where it is both (the relied-upon view).

Guided Path
1
Recognize the ambiguity of 'nadhr'
The term 'nadhr' is ambiguous: it can refer to a vow (a commitment to perform an act of worship, which becomes wajib) or an oath (a confirmation of a matter, which if broken, requires kaffarah). Intention resolves the ambiguity.
This is based on the principle that when a word is shared (mushtarak) between two meanings, the speaker's intent determines which meaning is intended.
2
List the six scenarios as per the text
The text enumerates six intentions: (1) no intention specific to fasting, (2) intention of nadhr only, (3) intention of nadhr and not an oath, (4) intention of oath and not nadhr, (5) intention of both, (6) intention of oath without reference to nadhr.
Scenarios 1-3 result in only a vow; scenario 4 results in only an oath; scenarios 5-6 result in both a vow and an oath.
3
Determine the ruling for each scenario
For scenarios 1-3: it is solely a nadhr (vow) by consensus. For scenario 4: it is solely an oath by consensus. For scenarios 5-6: it is both a nadhr and an oath, which is the relied-upon view (mufta bihi), contrary to a second opinion that says it's only one of them.
The 'second' opinion is referenced in the text: 'خلافاً للثاني' – it is unclear who is meant, but it indicates a weaker view.
4
State the consequences
If it is a nadhr only and broken, qada (making up) is required. If it is an oath only and broken, kaffarah (expiation) is required. If it is both, both qada and kaffarah are required.
Kaffarah is feed ten poor people or clothe them or free a slave; fasting three days if unable.
5
Note the basis: 'amal bil majaz'
The Hanafi ruling that scenarios 5-6 involve both nadhr and oath is based on acting on the general meaning of the metonymy (majaz). The word 'nadhr' is used in both its real (vow) and metaphorical (oath) sense when the intention is ambiguous.
This is a linguistic principle in usul al-fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصوم
سئل عن أفضل صلاة المرأة فقال : في أشد مكان من بيتها ظلمة. فعلى هذا ينبغي أنها إذا التزمت الصلاة في المسجد الحرام بالنذر فصلت في أشد مكان من بيتها ظلمة تخرج عن موجب نذرها على ما يقوله زفر رحمه الله وإن على الناذر النذر بشرط) كقوله : إن قدم زيد فلله علي أن أتصدق بكذا لا يجزيه عنه ما فعله قبل وجود شرطه) لأن المعلق بالشرط عدم قبل وجوده وإنما يجوز الأداء بعد وجود السبب الذي علق النذر به والله المنان بفضله.

Key Terms
النذر (al-nadhr): A verbal commitment to perform an act of worship which can function as a vow or an oath depending on intention.
اليمين (al-yamin): An oath, often by Allah, to do or not do something. Breaking it requires kaffarah.
المجاز (al-majaz): Metonymy; using a word in a non-literal sense. Here, 'nadhr' is used in both its literal (vow) and metaphorical (oath) senses.

Definition and Conditions of I'tikaf
Defines i'tikaf linguistically and legally, and states its conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi legal definition of i'tikaf, identify its conditions, and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the mosque requirement.

Core Idea
I'tikaf requires intention and a mosque with established congregation — the chosen Hanafi position.

I'tikaf is a profound act of worship with ancient roots, but its validity hinges on precise conditions. The Hanafi school refines these conditions based on the practice of the salaf, emphasizing the role of congregational prayer. This lesson unpacks the legal definition and the critical dispute over the mosque requirement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal definition
From the source, extract the legal definition: 'residence with intention in a mosque where congregation is actually established for the five prayers.' Note the linguistic roots.
The definition combines elements of physical dwelling and spiritual intent.
2
List the conditions for validity
Identify the conditions: (1) intention (niyyah), (2) mosque with established congregation for men, (3) for women: prayer area at home. Understand the rationale.
The condition of congregation is disputed within the school.
3
Locate the proof (dalil)
The source cites Quran 2:125 and the statement of Ali and Hudhayfa. Explain how these proofs support the condition.
The Quranic 'al-akifin' indicates legitimacy, but the hadith specifies congregation.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Contrast Abu Hanifa's view (masjid jam'iyyah required) with the Sahibayn (any mosque suffices). Note Abu Yusuf's distinction between obligatory and supererogatory i'tikaf.
Al-Saruji supported the Sahibayn's position.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The text declares 'ala al-mukhtar' (the chosen position) is that of Abu Hanifa. Understand the implications for fatwa.
The later Hanafi tradition follows Abu Hanifa.

Source Text

باب الاعتكاف
وجه المناسبة للصوم والتأخير عنه اشتراط الصوم في بعضه، والطلب الأكيد في العشر الأخير من رمضان وهو من الشرائع القديمة لقوله تعالى: أن طهرا بيتي للطائفين والعاكفين)

العكوف فالمتعدي بمعنى الحبس والمنع ومنه قوله تعالى : والهدي معكوفاً. ومنه الاعتكاف في المسجد لأنه حبس النفس ومنعها واللازم الإقبال على الشيء بطريق المواظبة ومنه قوله تعالى : يعكفون على أصنام لهم وشرعاً (هو الإقامة بنية) أي بنية الاعتكاف (في مسجد تقام فيه الجماعة بالفعل للصلاة الخمس لقول علي وحذيفة رضي الله عنهما : لا اعتكاف إلا في مسجد جماعة، ولأنه انتظار الصلاة على أكمل الوجوه بالجماعة (فلا يصح في مسجد لاتقام فيه الجماعة للصلاة في الأوقات الخمس على المختار) وعن أبي يوسف الاعتكاف الواجب لا يجوز في غير مسجد الجماعة، والنفل يجوز وهذا في حق الرجال (وللمرأة الاعتكاف في مسجد بيتها وهو محل عينته المرأة للصلاة فيه) فإن لم تعين لها

[الحج: ٢٢] قاله السيد قوله : (هو لغة اللبث) بفتح اللام وتضم المكث ا هـ در قوله : (وهو) أي الاعتكاف في حد ذاته لا بالمعنى المتقدم لأنه به يناسب اللازم، والمعنى أن فعله يأتي لازماً، ومتعدياً. قوله : (متعد) فيكون من باب ضرب ولازم فيكون من باب طلب ذكره السيد قوله : والهدى (معكوفاً أي محبوساً أي حبسه ومنعه الكفار سنة ست في الحديبية عن يبلغ محله، وهو الحرم. قوله : (لأنه حبس النفس أي على طاعة الله تعالى، وملازمة بيته، وقوله ومنعها أي عن الخروج عن المسجد، وعن المعاصي قوله: (وشرعاً هو الإقامة) هذا معنى اللازم، وقد جعل الاعتكاف في المسجد من المتعدى والظاهر أنه إن اعتبر فيه حبس النفس يأتي من المتعدى، وإن اعتبر فيه اللبث والإقامة يكون من اللازم. قوله : (بنية) سيأتي أن النية شرطه، فلا يحصل له ثوابه ولا يخرج عن واجبه بدونها قوله: (بالفعل) ظاهره، ولو يكون المقيم لها المعتكف وعبارة التنوير مع شرحه هو لبث ذكر في مسجد هو . ومؤذن أديت الخمس فيه أولاً، وعن الإمام اشتراط أداء الخمس فيه، وصححه بعضهم، وقال: يصح في كل مسجد، وصححه السروجي، وأما الجامع فيصح فيه مطلقاً اتفاقاً ا هـ فما ذكره المؤلف أحد قولين عن الإمام قوله: (ولأنه انتظار الصلاة (الخ أي فيختص بمكان يصلي فيه بالجماعة كذا في الشرح قوله : ( على أكمل (الوجوه متعلق بمحذوف صفة الصلاة، وقوله : بالجماعة تصوير لأكمل الوجوه قوله : ( على المختار) هذا مذهب الإمام، وقالا : يصح في كل مسجد، وصححه السروجي. قوله: (وعن أبي يوسف الخ) وجهه ظاهر فإن الواجب لا بد فيه من إقامة الصلاة في المسجد فاشتراط الجماعة له وجه وأما النفل فينتهي بالخروج، ولا يلزمه صلاة في المسجد فلا وجه لاشتراط الجماعة فيه قوله: (وللمرأة الاعتكاف في مسجد بينها ولا تخرج منه إذا اعتكفت فلو خرجت لغير عذر يفسد واجبه، وينتهي . نقله، ولو اعتكفت في المسجد فظاهر ما في النهاية أنه يكره تنزيهاً، وينبغي على قياس ما صرحوا به من أن المختار منعهن من الخروج في الصلوات كلها أن لا يتردد في منعهن من الاعتكاف في
لا المسجد قاله السيد:
Chapter of I'tikaf. The reason for its suitability with fasting and its placement after it is the requirement of fasting in some of it, and the emphatic seeking in the last ten days of Ramadan, and it is from the ancient laws due to His saying: 'Purify My House for those who circumambulate and those who stay in retreat.' (2:125) The verbal noun 'al-ukuf' is transitive meaning confinement and prevention, from which is His saying: 'and the sacrificial animal is confined.' (48:25) And from it is i'tikaf in the mosque because it is confinement of the self and prevention; the intransitive meaning is turning towards something by way of constancy, from which is His saying: 'they are devoted to their idols.' (7:138) And legally, it is 'residence with intention,' i.e., with the intention of i'tikaf, 'in a mosque where congregation is actually established for the five prayers,' due to the saying of Ali and Hudhayfa (may Allah be pleased with them): 'There is no i'tikaf except in a mosque of congregation,' and because it is waiting for prayer in the most complete manner by congregation. 'So it is not valid in a mosque where congregation for prayer is not established at the five times according to the chosen position.' And from Abu Yusuf: obligatory i'tikaf is not valid except in a mosque of congregation, but supererogatory i'tikaf is valid. And this applies to men. 'And for a woman, i'tikaf is in the mosque of her house, which is the place she designates for prayer.' If she does not designate... [then his saying: 'he has no imam' etc.] He said: (linguistically it is staying) with a fatha on the lam and with a damma on the meem, i.e., staying, as in Durr. His saying: ('and it') i.e., i'tikaf in itself, not in the aforementioned sense, because with it it suits the intransitive, and the meaning is that its action comes as intransitive and transitive. His saying: ('transitive') so it is from the pattern of daraba; and intransitive from the pattern of talaba, mentioned by al-Sayyid. His saying: ('confined') i.e., confined, i.e., the disbelievers prevented it in the year six at al-Hudaybiyyah from reaching its place, which is the Haram. His saying: ('because it is confinement of the self') i.e., in obedience to Allah, and staying in His house, and his saying ('prevention') i.e., from leaving the mosque and from sins. His saying: ('and legally it is residence') this is the intransitive meaning, and he has made i'tikaf in the mosque from the transitive; apparently if one considers confinement of the self, it comes as transitive, and if one considers staying and residence, it comes as intransitive. His saying: ('with intention') it will come that intention is its condition, so one does not attain its reward nor exit from its obligation without it. His saying: ('actually') apparently even if the one performing the iqama is the one in i'tikaf. And the expression of al-Tanwir and its commentary: it is staying mentioned in a mosque which and a caller to prayer performed the five prayers in it first. And from the Imam: the condition of performing the five prayers in it, and some corrected it, and he said: it is valid in every mosque, and al-Saruji corrected it. As for the masjid al-jami', it is valid in it absolutely by agreement. Ended. So what the author mentioned is one of two sayings from the Imam. His saying: ('because it is waiting for prayer' etc.) i.e., it is specific to a place where prayer is performed with congregation, as in the commentary. His saying: ('in the most complete manner') is related to an omitted description of prayer, and his saying ('by congregation') depicts the most complete manner. His saying: ('according to the chosen') this is the madhhab of the Imam, and they both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: it is valid in every mosque, and al-Saruji corrected it. His saying: ('and from Abu Yusuf etc.') its reasoning is apparent: for the obligatory, the establishment of prayer in the mosque is necessary, so requiring congregation has justification; as for supererogatory, it ends with exiting, and prayer in the mosque is not required, so there is no justification for requiring congregation. His saying: ('and for the woman, i'tikaf is in the mosque of her house') and she should not leave it when she observes i'tikaf; if she leaves without an excuse, it invalidates her obligatory i'tikaf and ends. This is transmitted. And if she observes i'tikaf in the mosque, apparently in al-Nihayah it is makruh tanzihan; and it is fitting, by analogy to what they have stated that the chosen opinion is to prevent them from going out for all prayers, that there should be no hesitation in preventing them from i'tikaf in the mosque. Al-Sayyid said.
Source pages p. 698

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on i'tikaf (spiritual retreat) in the Hashiya. It first explains why i'tikaf is placed after fasting in the text: because fasting is a condition for some i'tikaf (e.g., in the last ten days of Ramadan) and the practice is rooted in ancient divine law, citing the Quranic command to purify the Kaaba for those who perform i'tikaf (2:125). The commentary then distinguishes the two linguistic origins of 'akafa': transitive (to confine/restrain) and intransitive (to adhere constantly). The legal definition follows: 'residence with intention in a mosque where congregation is actually established for the five daily prayers.' This definition is built on the statement of Ali and Hudhayfa that i'tikaf is only valid in a mosque of congregation. The reason given is that i'tikaf involves waiting for prayer in the most complete manner via congregation. The 'al-mukhtar' (chosen) position of Imam Abu Hanifa is that i'tikaf is not valid in a mosque where the five daily congregational prayers are not held. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that any mosque suffices, and al-Saruji corrected this. Abu Yusuf further distinguishes: obligatory i'tikaf requires a mosque of congregation; supererogatory i'tikaf can be in any mosque. For women, i'tikaf is in the prayer area of her home; she must not leave it without excuse (invalidates obligatory i'tikaf). If a woman performs i'tikaf in a public mosque, it is considered makruh tanzihan (slightly disliked) by analogy with the ruling that she should be prevented from going out for prayers. The commentary also clarifies that intention is a condition for i'tikaf; without it, no reward or validity.

Key Terms
الاعتكاف (al-i'tikaf): Legal: residence with intention in a mosque where congregation is established for the five daily prayers, for the purpose of worship.
مسجد جماعة (masjid jamā'ah): A mosque where the five daily congregational prayers are held regularly with a congregation (even if the one in i'tikaf leads the prayer).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon Hanafi position regarding the mosque requirement for i'tikaf?
A) I'tikaf is valid in any mosque.
B) I'tikaf is only valid in a mosque where the five daily congregational prayers are held.
C) I'tikaf is valid only in the Prophet's Mosque in Medina.
D) I'tikaf is valid in any mosque for women and any mosque for men.

Key Takeaway
I'tikaf is valid only in a mosque with established five daily congregational prayers for men, and in the home prayer area for women, according to the mufta bihi Hanafi position.

Types of I'tikaf and Their Conditions
Explains division of i'tikaf and its conditions with proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three types of i'tikaf, identify the condition that distinguishes vowed i'tikaf, and explain the Hanafi position on Laylat al-Qadr with its proof.

Core Idea
I'tikaf is only obligatory by vow; its sunnah in Ramadan's last ten is proven by the Prophet's practice and the search for Laylat al-Qadr.

This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiya on Maraqi al-Falah divides i'tikaf into three categories and clarifies their legal status. It also delves into the contested issue of Laylat al-Qadr, showing how Hanafi usul resolves the ikhtilaf. Understanding these distinctions is essential for correctly performing i'tikaf with proper intention and conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types of i'tikaf and their hukm
Find the three categories: obligatory (wajib) for vowed i'tikaf, emphasized sunnah of sufficiency (sunnah mu'akkadah kifayah) for the last ten days of Ramadan, and recommended (mustahab) at other times. Note that the hukm changes based on vow or time.
2
Trace the dalil for sunnah i'tikaf in the last ten
The author cites the hadith of Jibril telling the Prophet to seek Laylat al-Qadr in the last ten, and the Prophet's practice of i'tikaf during those nights. Identify this as a dalil naqli (textual proof) for the sunnah ruling.
The hadith 'Seek it in the last ten and in every odd night' is also referenced.
3
Locate the ikhtilaf on Laylat al-Qadr and the Hanafi position
The passage presents the majority view that Laylat al-Qadr is fixed in the last ten, versus Abu Hanifa's view that it rotates through the year. Follow the Hanafi response using the interpretation that the hadith refers to that specific year.
The practical difference (thamarah) appears in vows tied to Laylat al-Qadr.
4
Extract the condition specific to vowed i'tikaf
The passage explicitly states 'Fasting is a condition for the validity of vowed i'tikaf.' Note that this condition does not apply to supererogatory i'tikaf. Also, the vow must be uttered (not mere intention).
The proof for the fasting condition is the Prophet's practice and hadith 'La i'tikafa illa bi-sawm' (weak, but supported by practice).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(والاعتكاف) المطلوب شرعاً على ثلاثة أقسام واجب في المنذور) تنجيزاً أو تعليقاً (وسنة) كفاية (مؤكدة في العشر الأخير . من رمضان) لاعتكافه العشر الأواخر من رمضان حتى توفاه الله ثم اعتكف أزواجه بعده لأنه لما اعتكف العشر الأوسط أتاه جبريل عليه الصلاة والسلام فقال : إن الذي تطلب أمامك يعني ليلة القدر فاعتكف العشر الأخير، وعن هذا ذهب الأكثر إلى أن ليلة القدر في العشر الأخير من رمضان منهم من قال في ليلة إحدى وعشرين ومنهم في سبع وعشرين، وفي الصحيح التمسوها في العشر الأواخر والتمسوها في كل وتر وعن أبي حنيفة أنها في رمضان، ولا يدري أي ليلة هي وقد تتقدم وقد تتأخر وعندهما كذلك إلا أنها معينة لا تتقدم ولا تتأخر والمشهور عن الإمام أنها تدور في السنة كما قدمناه في إحياء الليالي، وذكرت هنا طلباً للثواب، وقيل: في أوّل ليلة من رمضان وقيل : ليلة تسع وعشرين، وقال زيد بن ثابت : ليلة أربع وعشرين، وقال عكرمة : ليلة خمس وعشرين وأجاب أبو حنيفة عن لكونها في العشر الأواخر بأن المراد في ذلك الرمضان الذي التمسها عليه الصلاة والسلام فيه ومن علامتها أنها بلجة ساكنة لا حارة ولا قارّة تطلع الشمس صبيحتها بلا شعاع كأنها طشت، وإنما أخفيت ليجتهد في طلبها فينال بذلك أجر المجتهد في العبادة كما أخفى الله سبحانه الساعة ليكونوا على وجل من قيامها بغتة والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم (و) القسم الثالث (مستحب فيما سواه أي في أي وقت شاء سوى العشر الأخير ولم يكن منذوراً (والصوم شرط لصحة) الاعتكاف (المنذور) ولا نذر إلا بالنطق لأنه من متعلقات اللسان
And i'tikaf, legally desired, is of three types: obligatory in that which is vowed, immediate or conditional; and sunnah of sufficiency, emphasized in the last ten days of Ramadan, because he (Prophet) performed i'tikaf the last ten nights of Ramadan until Allah took him, then his wives performed i'tikaf after him, because when he performed i'tikaf the middle ten, Jibril came and said: 'That which you seek is before you,' meaning Laylat al-Qadr, so he performed i'tikaf the last ten. And from this, the majority held that Laylat al-Qadr is in the last ten of Ramadan; some say the twenty-first night, some the twenty-seventh. And in the Sahih: 'Seek it in the last ten, and seek it in every odd night.' And from Abu Hanifa that it is in Ramadan, and it is not known which night it is, and it may be early or late. And with them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) similarly, except that it is fixed, not early or late. And the well-known from the Imam is that it rotates through the year as we mentioned in Ihya al-Layali. And I mentioned it here seeking reward. And it is said: the first night of Ramadan, and it is said: the twenty-ninth. And Zayd ibn Thabit said: the twenty-fourth. And Ikrimah said: the twenty-fifth. And Abu Hanifa answered about it being in the last ten by saying that what is meant is that Ramadan in which the Prophet sought it. And among its signs: it is bright, calm, neither hot nor cold; the sun rises on its morning without rays, like a dish. And it was hidden so that one strives in seeking it and thus attains the reward of the one striving in worship, just as Allah hid the Hour so that they would be fearful of its sudden coming. And Allah knows best. And the third type is recommended in other times, meaning any time he wishes except the last ten, and it is not vowed. And fasting is a condition for the validity of vowed i'tikaf, and there is no vow except by utterance because it belongs to the tongue.
Source pages p. 700

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya of al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah details the types of i'tikaf (spiritual retreat in a mosque) and its conditions. The author first divides i'tikaf into three categories: 1) Wajib (obligatory) when one makes a vow (nathr) to perform it, whether the vow is immediate (e.g., 'I vow to do i'tikaf for three days') or conditional (e.g., 'If my father recovers, I will perform i'tikaf'). 2) Sunnah mu'akkadah kifayah (emphasized sunnah of sufficiency) during the last ten days of Ramadan, based on the Prophet's consistent practice until his death and his wives continuing afterwards. The proof is the hadith of Jibril instructing the Prophet to seek Laylat al-Qadr in the last ten days. 3) Mustahab (recommended) at any other time. The passage then discusses Laylat al-Qadr, noting that the majority hold it to be in the last ten, with various opinions on the exact night. Abu Hanifa's view is that it is in Ramadan but not fixed, and it may vary year to year; his associates (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold it is fixed but unknown. The well-known (mashhur) position from Abu Hanifa is that it rotates through the year, as mentioned earlier in the text. The signs of Laylat al-Qadr are given: calm, moderate temperature, and the sun rising without rays. The wisdom of its concealment is to encourage diligent worship. The passage concludes that fasting is a condition for the validity of vowed i'tikaf (but not for supererogatory i'tikaf according to the relied-upon position). The vow is only valid by utterance (not mere intention).

Key Terms
الاعتكاف (al-i'tikaf): Legal seclusion in a mosque with the intention of drawing closer to Allah.
ليلة القدر (Laylat al-Qadr): The Night of Decree, the night when the Quran was first revealed, better than a thousand months.
النذر (al-nathr): A vow to perform an act of worship, making it obligatory.
سنة كفاية (sunnah kifayah): A sunnah that is collective obligation; if enough people perform it, the rest are not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What condition distinguishes vowed i'tikaf from supererogatory i'tikaf according to this passage?
A) Fasting is required
B) It must be performed in Ramadan
C) It must be at least one day
D) It requires a mosque with congregational prayers

Key Takeaway
I'tikaf is a sunnah except when vowed, and the Hanafi school holds that Laylat al-Qadr is not fixed, rotating through Ramadan, which encourages year-long devotion.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Laylat al-Qadr: Fixed or Rotating?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on Laylat al-Qadr's fixity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on Laylat al-Qadr and apply the practical consequence to a vow scenario.

Core Idea
Laylat al-Qadr is hidden; Imams differ: Imam says it rotates, Sahibayn say it's fixed – a vow shows the difference.

In this passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi, the author delves into an internal Hanafi disagreement regarding the determination of Laylat al-Qadr. While the base text suggests the night may vary, the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) assert it is fixed, and Imam Abu Hanifa holds it rotates across years. The commentary explores the evidence and the practical implications for a vow, culminating in the mufta bihi ruling. This lesson unpacks that dispute.

Guided Path
1
State the two Hanafi positions
Identify the position of Imam Abu Hanifa (rotates) and the Sahibayn (fixed). Note the well-known (mashhur) view from Imam.
The source mentions 'المشهور عن الإمام' indicating the dominant transmission.
2
Identify the evidence for each position
Imam Abu Hanifa relies on the hadith of seeking it in the last ten days, interpreting it as specific to that Ramadan. The Sahibayn take the apparent general meaning.
The source states Imam responded: 'المراد في ذلك الرمضان الذي التمسها عليه الصلاة والسلام فيه'.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to the evidence
Explain how Imam Abu Hanifa's interpretation allows for rotation, while the Sahibayn insist on fixedness based on the same hadith.
The legal reasoning (istidlal) is based on whether the command is general or specific.
4
Derive the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Work through the vow scenario: if a master says 'you are free on Laylat al-Qadr' on the first night of Ramadan. Under Imam's view, the slave is not freed until the next Ramadan passes; under Sahibayn, freed after one night of the next Ramadan.
The source gives this as the benefit of the disagreement (فائدة الخلاف).
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Note that according to Al-Muhit, the fatwa is on Imam's view for a jurist who understands the ikhtilaf; for a layperson, it is the 27th night.
This shows the hierarchical authority in Hanafi fatwa.

أي المكلف مثلاً لقوله : بعد فينال
The beneficial evidences: It is known which night it is, and it may precede or lag behind. According to them (the two companions), it is specific, neither preceding nor lagging. The well-known position from the Imam is that it rotates in the year, as we have previously mentioned in Ihya' al-Layali. It is mentioned here seeking reward. It is said: on the first night of Ramadan, and it is said: the night of the twenty-ninth, and Zayd ibn Thabit said: the night of the twenty-fourth, and Ikrimah said: the night of the twenty-fifth. Abu Hanifah responded to it being in the last ten nights by saying that what is meant is that particular Ramadan in which the Prophet (peace be upon him) sought it. Among its signs: it is bright, calm, neither hot nor cold, and the sun rises on its morning without rays like a basin. It is concealed so that one strives in seeking it and thereby obtains the reward of the striving worshipper, just as Allah concealed the Hour so that they are in fear of its sudden occurrence. And Allah knows best. His statement: (According to them as well, i.e., in Ramadan, and the benefit of the disagreement: If he said to his slave: 'You are free on Laylat al-Qadr', and it was the first night of Ramadan, then according to him (Imam) he is not freed until the entire next Ramadan passes due to the possibility that it was the first night of the previous Ramadan and in the second its end. According to them, he is freed by the passing of one night of the next Ramadan because if it is always the first, then it has come, and if it is on other nights after it, then the previous Ramadan has covered it.) His statement: (The well-known from Imam, and it has been narrated from others as well. Al-Muhit said: The fatwa is on the Imam's statement, but he conditioned that one who takes an oath be a jurist who knows the disagreement; otherwise it is the night of the twenty-seventh.) His statement: (And I mentioned it here, i.e., I only mentioned it here despite the previous discussion on it in Ihya' al-Layali seeking reward, i.e., for my seeking reward by alerting to it through repetition.) His statement: (In that Ramadan, 'al' is for the present, i.e., the present Ramadan in which Jibril commanded the Prophet to seek it in the last ten.) His statement: (That it is bright, i.e., illuminated and luminous. In al-Qamus: a man with a bright face with sukun on the lam. It appears that 'baljah' here is with sukun, not with kasr.) His statement: (And not cold, i.e., cold, rather moderate.) His statement: (The sun rises... They mentioned that prayer during its night and its day is answered; if one misses its night, he can attain its day.) His statement: (Like a basin, with the dotted shin, and the sin with fatah on the ta and kasr in both. The ta may be replaced with sin and assimilated with the sin with fatah and kasr, so there are six variants.) His statement: (And it is only concealed... Just as the hour of answer on Friday is concealed so that one strives throughout it in worship, and just as the saint is concealed among the creation so that one thinks well of every Muslim and seeks blessings from him.) His statement: (So that he strives, with the verb in active voice for the responsible person, as he says later: 'then he obtains').
Source pages p. 701

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the determination of Laylat al-Qadr (the Night of Power). The base text (matn) states that its exact night is unknown and can precede or lag behind. However, the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that it is a fixed night that neither precedes nor lags. Imam Abu Hanifa's well-known position is that it rotates across the years. The commentary then elaborates on the practical consequence of this difference: if someone takes a vow to free a slave on Laylat al-Qadr, under the Imam's view the slave is not freed until the entire next Ramadan passes because the night could be in the previous or upcoming Ramadan. Under the companions' view, the slave is freed after one night of the next Ramadan. The commentary also reports from Al-Muhit that the fatwa (operative ruling) is on the Imam's view for a jurist who understands the disagreement; otherwise, the common practice is that it is the 27th night. Various opinions of the Companions and Successors are cited, and Abu Hanifa's response to the hadith placing it in the last ten days is that the hadith referred to a specific Ramadan. The signs of Laylat al-Qadr are described: a bright, calm night, moderate temperature, and the sun rising without rays. The wisdom behind its concealment is to encourage believers to strive in worship throughout Ramadan, similar to the concealment of the Hour of Answer on Friday and the hidden saints. The commentary also explains the meaning of 'baljah' (bright) and 'tasht' (basin) linguistically.

Key Terms
ليلة القدر (laylat al-qadr): A specific night in Ramadan whose exact date is unknown; it is more virtuous than a thousand months.
بلجة (baljah): Bright, luminous; refers to the night being well-lit.
طشت (tasht): A basin; the sun on the morning of Laylat al-Qadr appears without rays, likened to a basin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the vow scenario mentioned in the text, if the slave owner says 'you are free on Laylat al-Qadr' on the first night of Ramadan, what is the ruling according to Imam Abu Hanifa?
A) The slave is freed immediately.
B) The slave is freed after one night of the next Ramadan.
C) The slave is not freed until the entire next Ramadan passes.
D) The slave is never freed.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school internally disagrees on the fixity of Laylat al-Qadr, and the practical ruling on vows depends on which position is followed.

Excuses for Leaving Obligated I'tikaf and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on i'tikaf invalidation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which exiting obligatory i'tikaf does not invalidate it according to the Sahibayn, and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement with Imam Abu Hanifa.

Core Idea
Exiting obligatory i'tikaf for a valid necessity does not invalidate it according to the Sahibayn, but strict analogy (Imam) says it does.

Obligatory i'tikaf requires staying in the mosque with intention. But what if the mosque collapses or you are forced to leave? The Hanafi school has an internal dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two major students on the effect of such exits. This lesson unpacks the conditions for a valid excuse and the reasoning behind each position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute and its basis
Recognize that the passage presents an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding whether exiting for rare necessities invalidates obligatory i'tikaf.
Imam relies on qiyas; Sahibayn rely on istihsan.
2
List the valid excuses according to the Sahibayn
Extract from the text the specific excuses that the Sahibayn consider valid: collapse of the mosque, obligatory testimony, forcible expulsion, dispersal of family, fear of oppressors.
Also note the condition that the exit must be solely to continue i'tikaf elsewhere.
3
Apply the condition of immediacy and intent
Understand that after leaving for a valid excuse, the person must immediately go to another mosque and intend to continue i'tikaf. If he delays or does something else, it invalidates.
The intention is not necessarily per hour but for the whole journey.
4
Compare the dalil of both positions
Imam uses qiyas: any exit without valid excuse invalidates, and rarity does not change the rule. Sahibayn use istihsan: real needs override strict analogy.
The text mentions al-Kamal and al-Bahr discussing the tarjih.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon view for fatwa is that of the Sahibayn: exiting for these excuses does not invalidate i'tikaf.
Although al-Kamal preferred Imam's view, the majority and later scholars (al-Bahr, al-Nahr) favor Sahibayn.

أي بالعذر أي، وأما بغير العذر فيأثم لقوله تعالى: ﴿ولا تبطلوا أعمالكم﴾ [محمد : ٤٧] . قوله : (إذا) دام) أي كل منهما قوله: (وأتمه في المسجد) أما إذا خرج منه فعليه قضاؤه أيضاً لعدم وجود الركن قوله : (
